## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x and time t. In classical mechanics, the acceleration of an oscillator is determined by restoring forces (typically functions of position) and possibly damping or driving forces (functions of velocity/time). Nonlinear oscillators include Duffing, Van der Pol, and other anharmonic systems where the restoring force contains nonlinear terms in x.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator restoring force)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic oscillator)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodically driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driven Duffing with phase)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (nonlinear spring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force, exact pendulum)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Polynomial restoring + periodic drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (general driven Duffing)
- Power-law restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x * abs(x)**(c1) (generalized nonlinear restoring force)
- Combined quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power polynomial in x (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric restoring force typical of center-symmetric oscillators like Duffing
- Even-power terms in x (x**2) → broken symmetry in the potential, indicating asymmetric oscillator
- Sinusoidal dependence on t → external periodic driving force acting on the oscillator
- sin(x) or cos(x) restoring force → pendulum-like dynamics with bounded potential
- Product x * cos(c*t) → parametric excitation where stiffness is modulated in time
- Acceleration depending only on x (no explicit t) → autonomous/conservative oscillator system
- Polynomial in x with alternating signs → competing restoring and destabilizing forces creating multiple equilibria
- High-order odd polynomials dominating at large |x| → hardening or softening spring behavior

**GT: -1.15357x - 1.15357x·exp(-|x|) + 0.42262·sin(t)**

The key features of GT:
- A term proportional to sin(t)
- A term proportional to x
- A term proportional to x·exp(-|x|)

The function x·exp(-|x|) is the critical non-standard basis function. Let me analyze which candidates could potentially represent this.

**Key properties of x·exp(-|x|):**
- It's an odd function of x
- For small x: x·exp(-|x|) ≈ x - |x|·x + ... = x - x·|x| + ...
- It cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, tanh, sin, log, or combinations thereof over all x.

Let me check each candidate systematically:

**Candidates with tanh + polynomial/log/sin terms (1, 3, 4, 8, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, 16, 19, 21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28, 29, 33, 34, 36, 37, 38, 39, 40, 43, 44, 46, 53, 54, 55, 56, 57, 58):**

tanh(x) has a Taylor series x - x³/3 + 2x⁵/15 - ..., and x·exp(-|x|) has series x - |x|x + x²|x|/2 - ... The function x·exp(-|x|) involves |x| in a way that creates non-analytic behavior at x=0 (the function is smooth but its Taylor series structure differs). No finite combination of tanh, polynomials, sin, cos, log(x²+1), x^n can exactly equal x·exp(-|x|) for all x.

**Candidate 9:** c0*tanh(x) + c1*sin(t) + c2*x³ + c3*x + c4*x*|x|^c5

If c5 = 1, this gives x·|x| which is x² for x>0 and -x² for x<0. This is NOT x·exp(-|x|). No single power |x|^c5 can match exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 14:** c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*sin(c3*x) + c4*x*|x|^(1/3) — No, can't match.

**Candidate 17:** c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*x^c3 + c4*sin(t) — x^c3 is a single power, can't match exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 18:** c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*sin(t) + c3*x*|x|^c4 — Same issue, single power can't match.

**Candidates with rational functions (5, 6, 7):** These produce rational functions of x, not exponential decay. Cannot match.

**Candidates with polynomial + sin + log combinations (2, 15, 20, 31, 32, 35, 41, 42, 45, 47, 48, 49, 50, 51, 52):** None of these basis functions can produce x·exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 24:** Has x*exp(c6*x²) — this is exp of x², not exp(-|x|). Cannot match.

**Candidate 30:** Has x*exp(c6*x²) — same issue.

**Candidate 55:** Has exp(c5*x)*sin(c6*x) — this involves exp(c5*x), not exp(-|x|). Cannot match because exp(-|x|) is not analytic.

None of the candidates contain the basis function exp(-|x|) or any combination that could produce it exactly. The function x·exp(-|x|) is linearly independent from all basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials, tanh, sin, cos, log, rational functions, x^c power functions).
